                  <foreign lang="ar">عَصْر</foreign>: or, accord. to some, [it means <hi rend="ital">in the morning and the evening,</hi> or rather <hi rend="ital">in the forenoon and the afternoon,</hi> for they say that] it denotes constancy of religious service: Ibn-'Ámir and Aboo-'Abd-erRahmán Es-Sulamee read <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n31537-2" target="بِٱلْغُدْوَةِ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>وَٱلْعَشِىِّ</foreign>; but the former is the common reading; and A 'Obeyd says, we think that they read thus following the handwriting, for it is written in all the copies of the Kur-án with <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> like <foreign lang="ar">الصَّلَوة</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الزَّكَوة</foreign>, and this is not an indication of the reading [which they have adopted], as the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">الصلوة</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الزكوة</foreign> is not pronounced [otherwise than as an] of prolongation except that it requires the fet-hah that follows to be uttered with a somewhat broad sound]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ ٱبْنُ غَدَاتَيْنِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">He is a son of two days</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">he is two days old</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  The dim. is

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n31539-1" target="غَدْوَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n31538"/></foreign>, said by MF to be well known, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n31539-2" target="غِدْوَةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n31540"/></foreign>, said by him to be rare, or disapproved, (TA,) The <hi rend="ital">early part of the morning;</hi> the <hi rend="ital">first part of the day;</hi> (K;) or the <hi rend="ital">period between the time of the prayer of daybreak and sunrise;</hi> (S, Msb, K;) as also

(S, TA.) Zj says that when <foreign lang="ar">غُدْوَة</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">The</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بُكْرَة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">early part of the morning,</hi> &amp;c.,] <hi rend="ital">of the present day,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of a particular day,</hi> it is imperfectly decl.: and AHei says that it is thus accord. to the opinion commonly obtaining, as is also <foreign lang="ar">بُكْرَة</foreign>, each as being a generic proper name, like <foreign lang="ar">أُسَامَةُ</foreign>; and that when you mean to generalize, you say, <foreign lang="ar">غُدْوَةٌ وَقْتُ نَشَاطٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">An early part of a morning is a time of briskness, liveliness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sprightliness</hi>]; and when you mean to particularize, <foreign lang="ar">لَأَسِيرَنَّ اللَّيْلَةَ إِلَى غُدْوَةَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I will assuredly journey to-night until the early part of the morning</hi>]: (TA:) [in the latter case also] one says, <foreign lang="ar">أَتَيْتُهُ غُدْوَةَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I came to him in the early part of the morning of this,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of a particular, day</hi>]; <foreign lang="ar">غدوة</foreign> being here imperfectly decl. because it is determinate, like <foreign lang="ar">سَحَرَ</foreign>; but it is of those adv. ns. that may be used otherwise than as adv. ns.: you say, <foreign lang="ar">سِيرَ عَلَى فَرَسِكَ غُدْوَةَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">غُدْوَةً</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Journeying was performed on thy horse,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mare, in the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">غُدْوَة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">of this,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of a particular, day,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">in a</hi>

                  <foreign lang="ar">غُدْوَة</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">غَدَوِىٌّ</foreign> being a rel. n. from <foreign lang="ar">غَدٌ</foreign>: as though they rendered one desirous by saying, “ Our camels will bring forth and we will give thee to-morrow (<foreign lang="ar">غَدًا</foreign>): ” (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">غذو</foreign>, and TA:) what is thus termed is forbidden in a trad.: a man used to buy, for a camel or a she-goat or money, what was in the bellies of pregnant animals; and this is a hazardous proceeding, and was therefore forbidden. (Nh, TA.)
